                    <td>1/10/2017</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="rg badge">RG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/early-adp-thoughts-catcher-first-base/">Early ADP Thoughts – Catcher, First Base</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=11752">Paul Sporer</a></span></td></tr></table></div></td></tr>
            
            </table>
        </td>
        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
        
        <tr id="so2" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Year in Review: </b>After hitting 20 home runs in 227 at-bats in 2008, Napoli saw his playing time increase to 382 at-bats last year.  He enjoyed a fine season, albeit not nearly as productive as the previous year.  Napoli posted an .842 OPS in 2009, compared to a .960 mark a year earlier.  With the extra playing time he did not post the same rate stats, but Napoli was still one of the most productive catchers in the game.  He ranked fourth among all catchers with at least 300 at-bats with a .362 wOBA.   But while Napoli’s games played increased by 36, only 13 of those were extra starts behind the plate.  Manager Mike Scioscia still prefers the defense of Jeff Mathis, even though Mathis posted a .267 wOBA last year.  With Napoli catching, Angels pitchers had a 4.86 ERA and a 5.16 RA.  Those numbers were nearly a run lower with Mathis (3.99, 4.22) behind the plate.<br /><br /><b>The Year Ahead: </b>Scioscia praised Napoli’s defense late in the year, but will it translate to even more playing time in 2010?  Last year, Mathis was the primary catcher for Jered Weaver, John Lackey, and Ervin Santana while Napoli got most of the action with Joe Saunders on the hill.  When Scott Kazmir joined the club, Napoli got most of the starts.  If Lackey leaves as a free agent, that could open more starts for Napoli, especially since he did the bulk of the catching last year when Matt Palmer and Sean O’Sullivan pitched, the two likely internal candidates for the fifth starter’s job if Lackey exits.  Vladimir Guerrero’s departure would have led to more opportunities as a DH, but the club signed Hideki Matsui to fill that role.  Last year Napoli hit fewer fly balls and homered at a lesser rate than his career average.  With more playing time and regression to career norms, Napoli could challenge for 30 homers next year. (Brian Joura)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Napoli had quite the winter, getting shipped from Anaheim to Toronto and then on to Texas, where his arrival apparently contributed to Michael Young demanding a trade.  That's a lot of action for a guy who has never been a full-time player, but don’t be surprised if he’s also a hot commodity on draft day.  With power scarce at the catching position a new home park that should only enhance his ability to knock balls into the seats, Napoli should be near the top of the home run leaders among backstops in 2011.  However, that doesn’t mean you should go broke trying to put him on your roster.  His defense is poorly regarded enough that Ron Washington is unlikely to use him behind the plate all that frequently, and as of this writing, Michael Young is still a Ranger.  If Young sticks around in Texas, there won’t be an everyday job for Napoli, and he’ll end up filling a similar role to the one he had in Anaheim.  If you need power, he’s one to target, but know that he could end up sitting more than you might expect.  (Dave Cameron)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>A catcher who could hit 30 home runs or could end up as a platoon player who only gets 400 at-bats.  Keeper league owners should be aware that he probably won't have catcher eligibility for too many more years. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>"How do ya like me now, Scioscia?" No, Napoli didn't actually say that to his former Angels boss, but he might have wanted to. Never fully embraced in L.A., where he sometimes lost starts to aspiring Mendoza Line hitter Jeff Mathis, Napoli slashed .320/.414/.631, jacked 30 home runs and posted the best wOBA among hitters with 400+ PA (.444) after getting traded to Texas via Toronto. Only an oblique strain -- likely from knocking the bejesus out of the baseball so often -- slowed him down. Napoli managed to post career-best power numbers while simultaneously paring his strikeout rate, punching out just 19.7 percent of the time after doing so 25.7 percent in past years.  Chances are some of the two-strike adjustments he made will carry over to 2012. While Napoli is a legit top hitter, his batting average on balls in play was over 40 points above his career average and it might be stretching it to expect a .300+ isolated power again. Draft him expecting something in the range of .270/.370/.540. (David Golebiewski)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>With dual positional eligibility, newfound contact ability and home games in Arlington, Napoli is poised to keep on mashing. Just don't expect him to go all Jose Bautista on the league again in 2012. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Mike Napoli’s 2012 didn’t live up to his terrific 2011; his strikeout rate rose to an all-time high, and his wRC+ was the lowest it’s been since 2007. His strikeout rate is supremely confusing, since his underlying numbers do not suggest a ten-point swing in K%. Other than the strikeouts, Napoli’s numbers were pretty consistent with the rest of his career numbers, and it’s easy to see him having a bounceback in Boston. Fenway is going to be a good home for Napoli, and playing first base a vast majority of the time will help keep the right-hander happy and healthy. Since he’ll still be eligible at catcher, Napoli is worth at least a mid-round pick. The open question is when his hip condition will slow him down -- it's a risk to end his career. Don't overpay, considering. (Zach Sanders)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Mike Napoli had a down year in 2012, but he has a good chance to right the ship in Boston. He’s still worth at least a mid-round pick. As long as his hip's health holds.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>After some back-and-forth in the offseason regarding a latent hip injury, Mike Napoli's first season in Boston was a fairly successful one. The slugger carried over his catcher eligibility to finish among the top-five options at the position in 2013. Napoli saw both his walk and strikeout rates go the wrong the way, but just slightly, so there's no reason to sound the panic alarms of age-regression yet. Helping offset that, his batted ball distance jumped off 2012 lows and his line drive rate held steady at an impressive 24%. That's good news for his batting average on balls in play holding well north of .300, helping save some owners from his ugly whiff rate. While many expected him to post huge numbers at Fenway, he was surprisingly park-independent, although a return to Boston in 2014-2015 was probably the best news his owners could get this offseason. Unfortunately, his catcher eligibility will expire in 2014. No longer a top-five option in the catcher slot, his draft stock will plummet, although through no fault of his own. He still remains worthy of a first base or corner infield slot, but he's somewhat less exciting of a value play there. Also, while it sounds like his hip issues are under control, those in dynasty leagues would be smart to take his career one year at a time going forward.(<a href="http://www.twitter.com/soxczar">Colin Zarzycki</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>With Mike Napoli's days of donning the "tools of ignorance" behind him, his fantasy value will take a big hit in 2014. He's still worth snagging as a first baseman, but you'll need to wait much later if you want to scoop him up at good value.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>While his hips stayed intact, Mike Napoli found staying on the field consistently in 2014 to be somewhat problematic. The catcher-turned-first-baseman dislocated his left ring finger in April and it seemed to bother him all season. While both his walk rate and strikeout rate improved slightly over past seasons, the real nosedive came in the power department, with Napoli posting his first sub-.200 isolated slugging percentage in eight years. Fantasy owners hoping for 20+ dingers and 90+ RBI were left wanting, although those in OBP leagues certainly didn't hate the uptick to a .370 mark. The positives heading into 2015? Even with the nagging injuries, Napoli posted the second-highest contact rate of his career and his 304 foot fly ball distance was seventh-best in baseball (and a 10 foot improvement on 2013). More good chi? The righty slugger has had a full offseason to rest his finger and underwent bone-crunching (they literally broke his jaw) surgery to hopefully clear up chronic bouts of sleep apnea. Hey, those swanky hotels do little if you can't breathe, right? Look for Napoli has a bounce back candidate (albeit one with capped upside) later in drafts, with a few bumps up if you are in an on-base league. (Colin Zarzycki)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Mike Napoli never listened to Little League coaches who told him never to slide headfirst. Of course, this led to him dislocating a finger in April of last year which led to a precipitous drop in the power department. With a solid contact rate and top-ten fly ball distance, Napoli is a good candidate for a bounce back, even if he's an unsexy pick at first base.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Usually a model of consistency, Napoli's struggles out of the gate in Boston were a surprise to many fantasy owners (including me). It was great to see him perform so well down the stretch run if you are at all interested in getting cheap power on your roster at the end of drafts. Napoli was told he will be the regular first baseman in Cleveland this year, which will give him a decent leash to prove the start of last year was just a one-off blip rather than a trend. Napoli is no spring chicken and Cleveland is far from a power haven, but the power and patience combination could make him an intriguing "utility" option or corner infielder for leagues that feature that position. On top of being consistent with the bat, up until last year, Napoli has also maintained health of late. What I like about players in Napoli's mold is they usually come very cheap due to the overall numbers from the prior year, so cheap that if the struggles do occur again, he will be easy to drop and move on from. Napoli is more or less the epitome of that type of player entering this year. (Ben Duronio)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>No longer a 30 home run threat, Napoli will still have value as a utility or corner infield play as a source of power and on base percentage with the Indians.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>In 2016 Mike Napoli had a large spike in fly ball quality, resulting from a 3 mph increase in exit velocity, which served to increase both batting average and slugging on his fly balls. This manifested in the most valuable way possible - 16 more home runs. However, between his now 30% strike out rate and slow foot speed, his batting average will be decidedly below average. Napoli is entering his age 35 season as DH for the Rangers, where he should get a large number of plate appearances in a pretty strong line up. That said, Napoli will likely see his home run figures regress back to the 25 home runs per 600 plate appearances rate we've seen out of him for the majority of his career. (Andrew Perpetua)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Napoli needs to maintain his power numbers and accrue a lot of plate appearances in order to justify his fantasy value. A drop in either category could drop his home run total to 20 or fewer.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>

        }
        else {
            panelo.style.display = 'none';
            document.getElementById('soa2').style.fontWeight = 'normal';
        }
    }

    function setAverage(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_average') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == 'none') {
                                vis.display = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                vis.display = 'none';
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == 'none') {
                                vis.display = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                vis.display = 'none';
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

    function setMinorShow(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_minors_hide') {

                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

    function doNothing() { }

    function setPart(t) {
        var elements;
        var browserCheck = (document.all) ? 1 : 0;
        if (t == '*') {
            elements = (ie) ? document.all : document.getElementsByTagName('*');
        } else {
            elements = document.getElementsByTagName(t);
        }
        for (var i = 0; i < elements.length; i++) {
            var node = elements.item(i);
            var vis = elements.item(i).style;
            for (var j = 0; j < node.attributes.length; j++) {
                if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeName == 'class') {
                    if (node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_multi' || node.attributes.item(j).nodeValue == 'rgRow grid_multi') {


                        if (browserCheck > 0) {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'block';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'block') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'block'; }
                            }

                        }

                        else {

                            if (vis.display == undefined) {
                                vis.dispaly = 'table-row';
                            }
                            else {
                                if (vis.display == 'table-row') { vis.display = 'none'; } else { vis.display = 'table-row'; }
                            }

                        }

                    }
                }
            }
        }
    }

</script>

<script type="text/javascript">
    // Create the tooltips only on document load
    $(document).ready(function () {
        // Make sure to only match links to wikipedia with a rel tag
        $('a[tipgloss]').each(function () {
            // We make use of the .each() loop to gain access to each element via the "this" keyword...
            $(this).qtip(
		{
		    content: {
		        // Set the text to an image HTML string with the correct src URL to the loading image you want to use
		        text: " ",
		        ajax: {
		            url: $(this).attr('tipgloss') // Use the rel attribute of each element for the url to load
		        }
		    },
		    position: {
		        viewport: $(window),
		        at: "top center",
		        my: "bottom center",
		        effect: false
		    },
		    show: {
		        event: "click mouseenter",
		        solo: true // Only show one tooltip at a time
		    },
		    hide: {
		        event: "click mouseleave",
		        delay: 1000,
		        fixed: true
		    },
		    style: {
		        classes: "qtip-light"
		    }
		})

            // Make sure it doesn't follow the link when we click it
        });
    });
</script>
